     1	/*
     2	 * Active memory defragmentation
     3	 * Try to find key / value allocations that need to be re-allocated in order
     4	 * to reduce external fragmentation.
     5	 * We do that by scanning the keyspace and for each pointer we have, we can try to
     6	 * ask the allocator if moving it to a new address will help reduce fragmentation.
     7	 *
     8	 * Copyright (c) 2020, Redis Ltd.
     9	 * All rights reserved.

    49	#ifdef HAVE_DEFRAG
    50	
    51	typedef enum { DEFRAG_NOT_DONE = 0,
    52	               DEFRAG_DONE = 1 } doneStatus;
    53	
    54	/*
    55	 * Defragmentation is performed in stages.  Each stage is serviced by a stage function
    56	 * (defragStageFn).  The stage function is passed a target (void*) to defrag.  The contents of that
    57	 * target are unique to the particular stage - and may even be NULL for some stage functions.  The
    58	 * same stage function can be used multiple times (for different stages) each having a different
    59	 * target.
    60	 *
    61	 * The stage function is required to maintain an internal static state.  This allows the stage
    62	 * function to continue when invoked in an iterative manner.  When invoked with a 0 endtime, the
    63	 * stage function is required to clear it's internal state and prepare to begin a new stage.  It
    64	 * should return false (more work to do) as it should NOT perform any real "work" during init.
    65	 *
    66	 * Parameters:
    67	 *  endtime     - This is the monotonic time that the function should end and return.  This ensures
    68	 *                a bounded latency due to defrag.  When endtime is 0, the internal state should be
    69	 *                cleared, preparing to begin the stage with a new target.
    70	 *  target      - This is the "thing" that should be defragged.  It's type is dependent on the
    71	 *                type of the stage function.  This might be a dict, a kvstore, a DB, or other.
    72	 *  privdata    - A pointer to arbitrary private data which is unique to the stage function.
    73	 *
    74	 * Returns:
    75	 *  - DEFRAG_DONE if the stage is complete
    76	 *  - DEFRAG_NOT_DONE if there is more work to do
    77	 */
    78	typedef doneStatus (*defragStageFn)(monotime endtime, void *target, void *privdata);
    79	
    80	typedef struct {
    81	    defragStageFn stage_fn; // The function to be invoked for the stage
    82	    void *target;           // The target that the function will defrag
    83	    void *privdata;         // Private data, unique to the stage function
    84	} StageDescriptor;
    85	
    86	/* Globals needed for the main defrag processing logic.
    87	 * Doesn't include variables specific to a stage or type of data. */
    88	struct DefragContext {
    89	    monotime start_cycle;           // Time of beginning of defrag cycle
    90	    long long start_defrag_hits;    // server.stat_active_defrag_hits captured at beginning of cycle
    91	    list *remaining_stages;         // List of stages which remain to be processed
    92	    StageDescriptor *current_stage; // The stage that's currently being processed
    93	
    94	    long long timeproc_id;      // Eventloop ID of the timerproc (or AE_DELETED_EVENT_ID)
    95	    monotime timeproc_end_time; // Ending time of previous timerproc execution
    96	    long timeproc_overage_us;   // A correction value if over target CPU percent
    97	};
    98	static struct DefragContext defrag;
    99	
   100	
   101	/* There are a number of stages which process a kvstore.  To simplify this, a stage helper function
   102	 * `defragStageKvstoreHelper()` is defined.  This function aids in iterating over the kvstore.  It
   103	 * uses these definitions.
   104	 */
   105	/* State of the kvstore helper.  The private data (privdata) passed to the kvstore helper MUST BEGIN
   106	 *  with a kvstoreIterState (or be passed as NULL). */
   107	#define KVS_SLOT_DEFRAG_LUT -2
   108	#define KVS_SLOT_UNASSIGNED -1
   109	typedef struct {
   110	    kvstore *kvs;
   111	    int slot;
   112	    unsigned long cursor;
   113	} kvstoreIterState;
   114	/* The kvstore helper uses this function to perform tasks before continuing the iteration.  For the
   115	 * main hash table, large items are set aside and processed by this function before continuing with
   116	 * iteration over the kvstore.
   117	 *  endtime     - This is the monotonic time that the function should end and return.
   118	 *  privdata    - Private data for functions invoked by the helper.  If provided in the call to
   119	 *                `defragStageKvstoreHelper()`, the `kvstoreIterState` portion (at the beginning)
   120	 *                will be updated with the current kvstore iteration status.
   121	 *
   122	 * Returns:
   123	 *  - DEFRAG_DONE if the pre-continue work is complete
   124	 *  - DEFRAG_NOT_DONE if there is more work to do
   125	 */
   126	typedef doneStatus (*kvstoreHelperPreContinueFn)(monotime endtime, void *privdata);
   127	
   128	
   129	// Private data for main dictionary keys
   130	typedef struct {
   131	    kvstoreIterState kvstate;
   132	    int dbid;
   133	} defragKeysCtx;
   134	static_assert(offsetof(defragKeysCtx, kvstate) == 0, "defragStageKvstoreHelper requires this");
   135	
   136	// Private data for pubsub kvstores
   137	typedef hashtable *(*getClientChannelsFn)(client *);
   138	typedef struct {
   139	    getClientChannelsFn fn;
   140	} getClientChannelsFnWrapper;
   141	
   142	typedef struct {
   143	    kvstoreIterState kvstate;
   144	    getClientChannelsFn getPubSubChannels;
   145	} defragPubSubCtx;
   146	static_assert(offsetof(defragPubSubCtx, kvstate) == 0, "defragStageKvstoreHelper requires this");
   147	
   148	
   149	/* When scanning a main kvstore, large elements are queued for later handling rather than
   150	 * causing a large latency spike while processing a hash table bucket.  This list is only used
   151	 * for stage: "defragStageDbKeys".  It will only contain values for the current kvstore being
   152	 * defragged.
   153	 * Note that this is a list of key names.  It's possible that the key may be deleted or modified
   154	 * before "later" and we will search by key name to find the entry when we defrag the item later.
   155	 */
   156	static list *defrag_later;
   157	static unsigned long defrag_later_cursor;
   158	
   159	/* Defrag function which allocates and copies memory if needed, but DOESN'T free the old block.
   160	 * It is the responsibility of the caller to free the old block if a non-NULL value (new block)
   161	 * is returned.  (Returns NULL if no relocation was needed.)
   162	 */
   163	static void *activeDefragAllocWithoutFree(void *ptr, size_t *allocation_size) {
   164	    size_t size;
   165	    void *newptr;
   166	    if (!allocatorShouldDefrag(ptr)) {
   167	        server.stat_active_defrag_misses++;
   168	        return NULL;
   169	    }
   170	    /* move this allocation to a new allocation.
   171	     * make sure not to use the thread cache. so that we don't get back the same
   172	     * pointers we try to free */
   173	    size = zmalloc_size(ptr);
   174	    newptr = allocatorDefragAlloc(size);
   175	    memcpy(newptr, ptr, size);
   176	    if (allocation_size) *allocation_size = size;
   177	
   178	    server.stat_active_defrag_hits++;
   179	    return newptr;
   180	}
   181	
   182	/* Defrag helper for generic allocations.
   183	 *
   184	 * Returns NULL in case the allocation wasn't moved.
   185	 * When it returns a non-null value, the old pointer was already released
   186	 * and should NOT be accessed. */
   187	void *activeDefragAlloc(void *ptr) {
   188	    size_t allocation_size;
   189	    void *newptr = activeDefragAllocWithoutFree(ptr, &allocation_size);
   190	    if (newptr) allocatorDefragFree(ptr, allocation_size);
   191	    return newptr;
   192	}
   193	
   194	/* Defrag helper for sds strings
   195	 *
   196	 * Returns NULL in case the allocation wasn't moved.
   197	 * When it returns a non-null value, the old pointer was already released
   198	 * and should NOT be accessed. */
   199	sds activeDefragSds(sds sdsptr) {
   200	    void *ptr = sdsAllocPtr(sdsptr);
   201	    void *newptr = activeDefragAlloc(ptr);
   202	    if (newptr) {
   203	        size_t offset = sdsptr - (char *)ptr;
   204	        sdsptr = (char *)newptr + offset;
   205	        return sdsptr;
   206	    }
   207	    return NULL;
   208	}
   209	
   210	/* Performs defrag on a string-type (or generic) robj, but does not free the old robj.  This is the
   211	 * caller's responsibility.  This is necessary for string objects with multiple references.  In this
   212	 * case the caller can fix the references before freeing the original object.
   213	 */
   214	static robj *activeDefragStringObWithoutFree(robj *ob, size_t *allocation_size) {
   215	    if (ob->type == OBJ_STRING && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_RAW) {
   216	        // Try to defrag the linked sds, regardless of if robj will be moved
   217	        sds newsds = activeDefragSds((sds)ob->ptr);
   218	        if (newsds) ob->ptr = newsds;
   219	    }
   220	
   221	    robj *new_robj = activeDefragAllocWithoutFree(ob, allocation_size);
   222	
   223	    if (new_robj && ob->type == OBJ_STRING && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_EMBSTR) {
   224	        // If the robj is moved, correct the internal pointer
   225	        long embstr_offset = (intptr_t)ob->ptr - (intptr_t)ob;
   226	        new_robj->ptr = (void *)((intptr_t)new_robj + embstr_offset);
   227	    }
   228	    return new_robj;
   229	}
   230	
   231	
   232	/* Defrag helper for robj and/or string objects
   233	 *
   234	 * Returns NULL in case the allocation wasn't moved.
   235	 * When it returns a non-null value, the old pointer was already released
   236	 * and should NOT be accessed. */
   237	robj *activeDefragStringOb(robj *ob) {
   238	    size_t allocation_size;
   239	    if (ob->refcount != 1) return NULL; // Unsafe to defrag if multiple refs
   240	    robj *new_robj = activeDefragStringObWithoutFree(ob, &allocation_size);
   241	    if (new_robj) allocatorDefragFree(ob, allocation_size);
   242	    return new_robj;
   243	}
   244	
   245	/* Internal function used by zslDefrag */
   246	static void zslUpdateNode(zskiplist *zsl, zskiplistNode *oldnode, zskiplistNode *newnode, zskiplistNode **update) {
   247	    int i;
   248	    for (i = 0; i < zsl->level; i++) {
   249	        if (update[i]->level[i].forward == oldnode) update[i]->level[i].forward = newnode;
   250	    }
   251	    serverAssert(zsl->header != oldnode);
   252	    if (newnode->level[0].forward) {
   253	        serverAssert(newnode->level[0].forward->backward == oldnode);
   254	        newnode->level[0].forward->backward = newnode;
   255	    } else {
   256	        serverAssert(zsl->tail == oldnode);
   257	        zsl->tail = newnode;
   258	    }
   259	}
   260	
   261	/* Hashtable scan callback for sorted set. It defragments a single skiplist
   262	 * node, updates skiplist pointers, and updates the hashtable pointer to the
   263	 * node. */
   264	static void activeDefragZsetNode(void *privdata, void *entry_ref) {
   265	    zskiplist *zsl = privdata;
   266	    zskiplistNode **node_ref = (zskiplistNode **)entry_ref;
   267	    zskiplistNode *node = *node_ref;
   268	
   269	    /* defragment node internals */
   270	    sds newsds = activeDefragSds(node->ele);
   271	    if (newsds) node->ele = newsds;
   272	
   273	    const double score = node->score;
   274	    const sds ele = node->ele;
   275	
   276	    /* find skiplist pointers that need to be updated if we end up moving the
   277	     * skiplist node. */
   278	    zskiplistNode *update[ZSKIPLIST_MAXLEVEL];
   279	    zskiplistNode *x = zsl->header;
   280	    for (int i = zsl->level - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
   281	        /* stop when we've reached the end of this level or the next node comes
   282	         * after our target in sorted order */
   283	        zskiplistNode *next = x->level[i].forward;
   284	        while (next &&
   285	               (next->score < score ||
   286	                (next->score == score && sdscmp(next->ele, ele) < 0))) {
   287	            x = next;
   288	            next = x->level[i].forward;
   289	        }
   290	        update[i] = x;
   291	    }
   292	    /* should have arrived at intended node */
   293	    serverAssert(x->level[0].forward == node);
   294	
   295	    /* try to defrag the skiplist record itself */
   296	    zskiplistNode *newnode = activeDefragAlloc(node);
   297	    if (newnode) {
   298	        zslUpdateNode(zsl, node, newnode, update);
   299	        *node_ref = newnode; /* update hashtable pointer */
   300	    }
   301	}
   302	
   303	#define DEFRAG_SDS_DICT_NO_VAL 0
   304	#define DEFRAG_SDS_DICT_VAL_IS_SDS 1
   305	#define DEFRAG_SDS_DICT_VAL_IS_STROB 2
   306	#define DEFRAG_SDS_DICT_VAL_VOID_PTR 3
   307	#define DEFRAG_SDS_DICT_VAL_LUA_SCRIPT 4
   308	
   309	static void activeDefragSdsDictCallback(void *privdata, const dictEntry *de) {
   310	    UNUSED(privdata);
   311	    UNUSED(de);
   312	}
   313	
   314	/* Defrag a dict with sds key and optional value (either ptr, sds or robj string) */
   315	static void activeDefragSdsDict(dict *d, int val_type) {
   316	    unsigned long cursor = 0;
   317	    dictDefragFunctions defragfns = {
   318	        .defragAlloc = activeDefragAlloc,
   319	        .defragKey = (dictDefragAllocFunction *)activeDefragSds,
   320	        .defragVal = (val_type == DEFRAG_SDS_DICT_VAL_IS_SDS       ? (dictDefragAllocFunction *)activeDefragSds
   321	                      : val_type == DEFRAG_SDS_DICT_VAL_IS_STROB   ? (dictDefragAllocFunction *)activeDefragStringOb
   322	                      : val_type == DEFRAG_SDS_DICT_VAL_VOID_PTR   ? (dictDefragAllocFunction *)activeDefragAlloc
   323	                      : val_type == DEFRAG_SDS_DICT_VAL_LUA_SCRIPT ? (dictDefragAllocFunction *)evalActiveDefragScript
   324	                                                                   : NULL)};
   325	    do {
   326	        cursor = dictScanDefrag(d, cursor, activeDefragSdsDictCallback, &defragfns, NULL);
   327	    } while (cursor != 0);
   328	}
   329	
   330	static void activeDefragSdsHashtableCallback(void *privdata, void *entry_ref) {
   331	    UNUSED(privdata);
   332	    sds *sds_ref = (sds *)entry_ref;
   333	    sds new_sds = activeDefragSds(*sds_ref);
   334	    if (new_sds != NULL) *sds_ref = new_sds;
   335	}
   336	
   337	/* Defrag a list of ptr, sds or robj string values */
   338	static void activeDefragQuickListNode(quicklist *ql, quicklistNode **node_ref) {
   339	    quicklistNode *newnode, *node = *node_ref;
   340	    unsigned char *newzl;
   341	    if ((newnode = activeDefragAlloc(node))) {
   342	        if (newnode->prev)
   343	            newnode->prev->next = newnode;
   344	        else
   345	            ql->head = newnode;
   346	        if (newnode->next)
   347	            newnode->next->prev = newnode;
   348	        else
   349	            ql->tail = newnode;
   350	        *node_ref = node = newnode;
   351	    }
   352	    if ((newzl = activeDefragAlloc(node->entry))) node->entry = newzl;
   353	}
   354	
   355	static void activeDefragQuickListNodes(quicklist *ql) {
   356	    quicklistNode *node = ql->head;
   357	    while (node) {
   358	        activeDefragQuickListNode(ql, &node);

  1018	        serverAssert(!defrag.current_stage);
  1019	        serverAssert(listLength(defrag.remaining_stages) == 0);

  1058	/* Must be called at the start of the timeProc as it measures the delay from the end of the previous
  1059	 * timeProc invocation when performing the computation. */
  1060	static int computeDefragCycleUs(void) {
  1061	    long dutyCycleUs;
  1062	
  1063	    int targetCpuPercent = server.active_defrag_cpu_percent;
  1064	    serverAssert(targetCpuPercent > 0 && targetCpuPercent < 100);
  1065	
  1066	    static int prevCpuPercent = 0; // STATIC - this persists
  1067	    if (targetCpuPercent != prevCpuPercent) {
  1068	        /* If the targetCpuPercent changes, the value might be different from when the last wait
  1069	         *  time was computed.  In this case, don't consider wait time.  (This is really only an
  1070	         *  issue in crazy tests that dramatically increase CPU while defrag is running.) */
  1071	        defrag.timeproc_end_time = 0;
  1072	        prevCpuPercent = targetCpuPercent;
  1073	    }
  1074	
  1075	    // Given when the last duty cycle ended, compute time needed to achieve the desired percentage.
  1076	    if (defrag.timeproc_end_time == 0) {
  1077	        // Either the first call to the timeProc, or we were paused for some reason.
  1078	        defrag.timeproc_overage_us = 0;
  1079	        dutyCycleUs = server.active_defrag_cycle_us;
  1080	    } else {
  1081	        long waitedUs = getMonotonicUs() - defrag.timeproc_end_time;
  1082	        /* Given the elapsed wait time between calls, compute the necessary duty time needed to
  1083	         *  achieve the desired CPU percentage.
  1084	         *  With:  D = duty time, W = wait time, P = percent
  1085	         *  Solve:    D          P
  1086	         *          -----   =  -----
  1087	         *          D + W       100
  1088	         *  Solving for D:
  1089	         *     D = P * W / (100 - P)
  1090	         *
  1091	         * Note that dutyCycleUs addresses starvation.  If the wait time was long, we will compensate
  1092	         *  with a proportionately long duty-cycle.  This won't significantly affect perceived
  1093	         *  latency, because clients are already being impacted by the long cycle time which caused
  1094	         *  the starvation of the timer. */
  1095	        dutyCycleUs = targetCpuPercent * waitedUs / (100 - targetCpuPercent);
  1096	
  1097	        // Also adjust for any accumulated overage.
  1098	        dutyCycleUs -= defrag.timeproc_overage_us;
  1099	        defrag.timeproc_overage_us = 0;
  1100	
  1101	        if (dutyCycleUs < server.active_defrag_cycle_us) {
  1102	            /* We never reduce our cycle time, that would increase overhead.  Instead, we track this
  1103	             *  as part of the overage, and increase wait time between cycles. */
  1104	            defrag.timeproc_overage_us = server.active_defrag_cycle_us - dutyCycleUs;
  1105	            dutyCycleUs = server.active_defrag_cycle_us;
  1106	        }
  1107	    }
  1108	    return dutyCycleUs;
  1109	}
  1110	
  1111	
  1112	/* Must be called at the end of the timeProc as it records the timeproc_end_time for use in the next
  1113	 * computeDefragCycleUs computation. */
  1114	static int computeDelayMs(monotime intendedEndtime) {
  1115	    defrag.timeproc_end_time = getMonotonicUs();
  1116	    long overage = defrag.timeproc_end_time - intendedEndtime;
  1117	    defrag.timeproc_overage_us += overage; // track over/under desired CPU
  1118	    /* Allow negative overage (underage) to count against existing overage, but don't allow
  1119	     * underage (from short stages) to be accumulated.  */
  1120	    if (defrag.timeproc_overage_us < 0) defrag.timeproc_overage_us = 0;
  1121	
  1122	    int targetCpuPercent = server.active_defrag_cpu_percent;
  1123	    serverAssert(targetCpuPercent > 0 && targetCpuPercent < 100);
  1124	
  1125	    // Given the desired duty cycle, what inter-cycle delay do we need to achieve that?
  1126	    // We want to achieve a specific CPU percent.  To do that, we can't use a skewed computation.
  1127	    // Example, if we run for 1ms and delay 10ms, that's NOT 10%, because the total cycle time is 11ms.
  1128	    // Instead, if we rum for 1ms, our total time should be 10ms.  So the delay is only 9ms.
  1129	    long totalCycleTimeUs = server.active_defrag_cycle_us * 100 / targetCpuPercent;
  1130	    long delayUs = totalCycleTimeUs - server.active_defrag_cycle_us;
  1131	    // Only increase delay by the fraction of the overage that would be non-duty-cycle
  1132	    delayUs += defrag.timeproc_overage_us * (100 - targetCpuPercent) / 100;
  1133	    if (delayUs < 0) delayUs = 0;
  1134	    long delayMs = delayUs / 1000; // round down
  1135	    return delayMs;
  1136	}

  1175	            serverAssert(status == DEFRAG_NOT_DONE); // Initialization should always return DEFRAG_NOT_DONE
  1176	        }
  1177	
  1178	        doneStatus status = defrag.current_stage->stage_fn(endtime, defrag.current_stage->target, defrag.current_stage->privdata);
  1179	        if (status == DEFRAG_DONE) {
  1180	            zfree(defrag.current_stage);
  1181	            defrag.current_stage = NULL;
  1182	        }
  1183	
  1184	        haveMoreWork = (defrag.current_stage || listLength(defrag.remaining_stages) > 0);
  1185	        /* If we've completed a stage early, and still have a standard time allotment remaining,
  1186	         * we'll start another stage.  This can happen when defrag is running infrequently, and
  1187	         * starvation protection has increased the duty-cycle. */
  1188	    } while (haveMoreWork && getMonotonicUs() <= endtime - server.active_defrag_cycle_us);
  1189	
  1190	    latencyEndMonitor(latency);
  1191	    latencyAddSampleIfNeeded("active-defrag-cycle", latency);
  1192	    latencyTraceIfNeeded(db, active_defrag_cycle, latency);
  1193	    if (haveMoreWork) {
  1194	        return computeDelayMs(endtime);
  1195	    } else {
  1196	        endDefragCycle(true);
  1197	        return AE_NOMORE; // Ends the timer proc
  1198	    }
  1199	}
  1200	
  1201	
  1202	/* During long running scripts, or while loading, there is a periodic function for handling other
  1203	 * actions.  This interface allows defrag to continue running, avoiding a single long defrag step
  1204	 * after the long operation completes. */
  1205	void defragWhileBlocked(void) {
  1206	    // This is called infrequently, while timers are not active.  We might need to start defrag.
  1207	    if (!defragIsRunning()) monitorActiveDefrag();
  1208	
  1209	    if (!defragIsRunning()) return;
  1210

     1	proc test_memory_efficiency {range} {
     2	    r flushall
     3	    set rd [valkey_deferring_client]
     4	    set base_mem [s used_memory]
     5	    set written 0
     6	    for {set j 0} {$j < 10000} {incr j} {
     7	        set key key:$j
     8	        set val [string repeat A [expr {int(rand()*$range)}]]
     9	        $rd set $key $val
    10	        incr written [string length $key]
    11	        incr written [string length $val]
    12	        incr written 2 ;# A separator is the minimum to store key-value data.
    13	    }
    14	    for {set j 0} {$j < 10000} {incr j} {
    15	        $rd read ; # Discard replies
    16	    }
    17	
    18	    set current_mem [s used_memory]
    19	    set used [expr {$current_mem-$base_mem}]
    20	    set efficiency [expr {double($written)/$used}]
    21	    return $efficiency
    22	}

    40	run_solo {defrag} {
    41	    # make logging a bit more readable
    42	    proc to_mb {bytes} {
    43	        return [format "%6.2f MB" [expr $bytes / 1024.0 / 1024.0]]
    44	    }
    45	
    46	    # Utility function used to create a sequence where each key has an increasing
    47	    # number of fields/values.  For each key, the number for fields/values will
    48	    # increase by 2x.  Key 0 will have 2 values, key 1 will have 4, key 2 will
    49	    # have 8, etc.  Pass in the previous key/field pair to get the next.
    50	    # The sequence is: (0,0), (0,1), (1,0), (1,1), (1,2), (1,3), (2,0)...
    51	    # The optional 'incby' parameter allows incrementing by 2 across the sequence.
    52	    proc next_exp_kf {key field {incby 1}} {
    53	        assert {$incby == 1 || $incby == 2}
    54	        incr field $incby
    55	        if {$field == 2 ** ($key+1)} {
    56	            incr key
    57	            set field 0
    58	        }
    59	        return [list $key $field]
    60	    }
    61	
    62	    # Make a deferring client with CLIENT REPLY OFF sync with the server by
    63	    # temporarily setting CLIENT REPLY ON and waiting for the reply, then
    64	    # switching back to CLIENT REPLY OFF.
    65	    proc client_reply_off_wait_for_server {rd} {
    66	        $rd client reply on
    67	        assert_equal OK [$rd read]
    68	        $rd client reply off
    69	    }
    70	
    71	    # Logs defragging state if ::verbose is true
    72	    proc log_frag {title} {
    73	        # Note, this delay is outside of the "if" so that behavior is the same, with and
    74	        #  without verbose logging.  Also, this allows for assertions to follow without
    75	        #  adding additional delay statements
    76	        after 120  ;# serverCron only updates the info once in 100ms
    77	        if {$::verbose} {
    78	            puts "Frag info: $title"
    79	            puts "    used: [to_mb [s allocator_allocated]]"
    80	            puts "    frag: [to_mb [s allocator_frag_bytes]]"
    81	            puts "    frag ratio: [s allocator_frag_ratio]"
    82	            puts "    hits: [s active_defrag_hits]"
    83	            puts "    misses: [s active_defrag_misses]"
    84	        }
    85	    }
    86	
    87	    # Start defrag and wait for it to stop
    88	    # The optional code block is executed after defrag has started
    89	    proc perform_defrag {{code_block {}}} {
    90	        r config set latency-monitor-threshold 5
    91	        r latency reset
    92	
    93	        set old_defrag_time [s total_active_defrag_time]
    94	        r config set activedefrag yes
    95	
    96	        # Wait for defrag to start
    97	        wait_for_condition 10 50 {
    98	            [s total_active_defrag_time] ne $old_defrag_time
    99	        } else {
   100	            log_frag "defrag not started"
   101	            puts [r info memory]
   102	            puts [r info stats]
   103	            puts [r memory malloc-stats]
   104	            fail "defrag not started."
   105	        }
   106	
   107	        # Execute the passed in code block
   108	        uplevel 1 $code_block
   109	
   110	        # Wait for the active defrag to stop working.
   111	        wait_for_condition 150 200 {
   112	            [s active_defrag_running] eq 0
   113	        } else {
   114	            log_frag "defrag didn't stop"
   115	            puts [r info memory]
   116	            puts [r memory malloc-stats]
   117	            fail "defrag didn't stop."
   118	        } debug {
   119	            log_frag "defragging..."
   120	        }
   121	
   122	        r config set activedefrag no
   123	        after 120 ;# ensure memory stats are current when function exits
   124	    }
   125	
   126	    # Checks for any significant latency events
   127	    proc validate_latency {limit_ms} {
   128	        if {!$::no_latency} {
   129	            set max_latency 0
   130	            foreach event [r latency latest] {
   131	                lassign $event eventname time latency max
   132	                if {$eventname == "active-defrag-cycle" || $eventname == "while-blocked-cron"} {
   133	                    set max_latency $max
   134	                }
   135	            }
   136	            if {$::verbose} {
   137	                puts "Validating max latency ($max_latency) is LT $limit_ms"
   138	                if {$max_latency > 0} {
   139	                    puts [r latency latest]
   140	                    puts [r latency history active-defrag-cycle]
   141	                    puts [r latency history while-blocked-cron]
   142	                }
   143	            }
   144	            assert {$max_latency <= $limit_ms}
   145	        }
   146	    }
   147	
   148	    # Validate expected fragmentation ratio
   149	    # op = "<" (less than) or ">" (greater than)
   150	    proc validate_frag_ratio {op value} {
   151	        set frag [s allocator_frag_ratio]
   152	        if {$::verbose} {
   153	            puts "Validating frag ($frag) $op $value"
   154	        }
   155	        set allocated_bytes [s allocator_allocated]
   156	        if {$allocated_bytes < 20 * 1024 * 1024} {
   157	            # If allocated bytes is too small, the ratios get wonky.  Since we use 2MB for
   158	            # active-defrag-ignore-bytes, let's make sure that we have at least 10x that amount
   159	            # allocated before trying to verify any fragmentation ratios.  Otherwise the tests
   160	            # are likely to get flaky.
   161	            error "test error: trying to validate frag ratio with only $allocated_bytes allocated"
   162	        }
   163	        if {$op == "<"} {
   164	            assert_lessthan $frag $value
   165	        } elseif {$op == ">"} {
   166	            assert_morethan $frag $value
   167	        } else {
   168	            error "Operator value($op) must be '<' or '>'"
   169	        }
   170	    }
   171	
   172	    # Performs a standardized defrag test.  The "populate" block generates data.  The "fragment" block
   173	    # fragments that data (usually by deleting half).
   174	    #  - caller must generate at least 40 MB of data
   175	    #  - after fragmentation, at least 20 MB of data must remain, and fragmentation ratio must exceed 1.4
   176	    # Positional parameters:
   177	    #    name - name of the test
   178	    # Named parameters:
   179	    #    populate {code} - required, populates initial unfragmented data
   180	    #    fragment {code} - required, fragments the populated data
   181	    #    while_defragging {code} - optional, code executed after defrag has started
   182	    #    latency <ms> - optional, verifies the latency to a ms target (default 5)
   183	    proc perform_defrag_test {name args} {
   184	        # This value should be 5 ms, but it was flaky in github runners. The issue 
   185	        # https://github.com/valkey-io/valkey/issues/2444 is tracking if we can raise the limit again.
   186	        set opts(latency) 40
   187	        set opts(while_defragging) {}
   188	        array set opts $args
   189	        assert {[info exists opts(populate)]}
   190	        assert {[info exists opts(fragment)]}
   191	
   192	        r config set active-defrag-threshold-lower 5
   193	        r config set active-defrag-cycle-min 40
   194	        r config set active-defrag-cycle-max 60
   195	        r config set active-defrag-ignore-bytes 2500kb
   196	        r config set maxmemory 0
   197	
   198	        log_frag "test start ($name)"
   199	
   200	        # at this point, we expect fragmentation BYTES to be below a threshold
   201	        #  (percentage is wildly variable with low memory usage)
   202	        assert {[s allocator_frag_bytes] < 2 * 1024 * 1024}
   203	
   204	        # populate the DB with data
   205	        set initial_allocated [s allocator_allocated]
   206	        uplevel 1 $opts(populate)
   207	
   208	        log_frag "after adding data"
   209	        # check that enough data has been populated
   210	        set required [expr 50 * 1024 * 1024]
   211	        set allocated [expr [s allocator_allocated] - $initial_allocated]
   212	        if {$allocated < $required} {
   213	            fail "Tests are required to create at least $required bytes of data before fragmentation - only $allocated bytes created"
   214	        }
   215	        # check that at this point, fragmentation is very low
   216	        validate_frag_ratio < 1.05
   217	
   218	        # fragment the data
   219	        uplevel 1 $opts(fragment)
   220	
   221	        log_frag "after fragmenting data"
   222	        # we want some fragmentation, but we still want a minimum allocation
   223	        validate_frag_ratio > 1.4
   224	        set required [expr 25 * 1024 * 1024]
   225	        set allocated [expr [s allocator_allocated] - $initial_allocated]
   226	        if {$allocated < $required} {
   227	            fail "Tests are required to retain at least $required bytes of data after fragmentation - only $allocated bytes retained"
   228	        }
   229	
   230	        set digest [debug_digest]
   231	
   232	        perform_defrag $opts(while_defragging)
   233	
   234	        log_frag "after defragging"
   235	        validate_frag_ratio < 1.1
   236	        validate_latency $opts(latency)
   237	
   238	        # verify the data isn't corrupted or changed
   239	        set newdigest [debug_digest]
   240	        assert {$digest eq $newdigest}
   241	        r save ;# saving an rdb iterates over all the data / pointers
   242	    }
   243	
   244	    proc test_main_dictionary {type} {
   245	        set title "Active Defrag main dictionary: $type"
   246	        test $title {
   247	            set n 200000
   248	
   249	            perform_defrag_test $title populate {
   250	                # add a mass of string keys
   251	                set rd [valkey_deferring_client]
   252	                $rd client reply off
   253	                for {set j 0} {$j < $n} {incr j} {
   254	                    $rd setrange $j 250 a
   255	                    if {$j % 3 == 0} {
   256	                        $rd expire $j 1000 ;# put expiration on some
   257	                    }
   258	                    if {$j % 1000 == 999} {client_reply_off_wait_for_server $rd}
   259	                }
   260	                assert {[scan [regexp -inline {expires\=([\d]*)} [r info keyspace]] expires=%d] > 0}
   261	            } fragment {
   262	                # delete half of the keys
   263	                for {set j 0} {$j < $n} {incr j 2} {
   264	                    $rd del $j
   265	                    if {$j % 1000 == 998} {client_reply_off_wait_for_server $rd}
   266	                }
   267	                $rd close
   268	
   269	                # use custom slower defrag speed to start so that while_defragging has time
   270	                r config set active-defrag-cycle-min 2
   271	                r config set active-defrag-cycle-max 3
   272	            } while_defragging {
   273	                # This test runs for a while, during this interval, we verify changing the CPU range.
   274	                set current_cpu [s active_defrag_running]
   275	                assert_range $current_cpu 2 3
   276	
   277	                # alter the CPU limits and check that they took effect
   278	                r config set active-defrag-cycle-min 1
   279	                r config set active-defrag-cycle-max 1
   280	                after 120
   281	                # it's possible that defrag has already completed
   282	                assert {[s active_defrag_running] == 1}
   283	
   284	                # now bump up the CPU to finish quickly
   285	                r config set active-defrag-cycle-min 40
   286	                r config set active-defrag-cycle-max 60
   287	            }
   288	
   289	            # in standalone mode, test AOF loading too (using the remaining data from the section above)
   290	            if {$type eq "standalone"} {
   291	            test "Active defrag - AOF loading" {
   292	                # reset stats and load the AOF file
   293	                r config resetstat
   294	                r config set key-load-delay -25 ;# sleep on average 1/25 usec
   295	                # Note: This test is checking if defrag is working DURING AOF loading (while
   296	                #       timers are not active).  So we don't give any extra time, and we deactivate
   297	                #       defrag immediately after the AOF loading is complete.  During loading,
   298	                #       defrag will get invoked less often, causing starvation prevention.  We
   299	                #       should expect longer latency measurements.
   300	                r config set active-defrag-cycle-min 50
   301	                r config set active-defrag-cycle-max 50
   302	                r config set activedefrag yes
   303	                r debug loadaof
   304	                r config set activedefrag no
   305	                after 50 ;# give defrag time to stop
   306	
   307	                log_frag "after AOF loading"
   308	
   309	                # The AOF contains simple (fast) SET commands (and the cron during loading runs every 1024 commands).
   310	                # Even so, defrag can get starved for periods exceeding 100ms.  Using 200ms for test stability, and
   311	                # a 50% CPU requirement, we should allow up to 200ms latency
   312	                # (as total time = 200 non duty + 200 duty = 400ms, and 50% of 400ms is 200ms).
   313	                validate_latency 200
   314	
   315	                # Make sure we had defrag hits during AOF loading.  Note that we don't worry about
   316	                # the actual fragmentation ratio here.  It will vary based on when defrag stopped
   317	                # mid-cycle.  Just check that we are defragging by the number of hits.
   318	                assert {[s active_defrag_hits] > 80000}
   319	            }
   320	            } ;# Active defrag - AOF loading
   321	        }
   322	    }

   324	    proc test_eval_scripts {type} {
   325	        set title "Active Defrag eval scripts: $type"
   326	        test $title {
   327	            set n 50000
   328	
   329	            # scripts aren't defragged incrementally, expect big latency
   330	            perform_defrag_test $title latency 200 populate {
   331	                # Populate memory with interleaving script-key pattern of same size
   332	                set dummy_script "--[string repeat x 450]\nreturn "
   333	                set rd [valkey_deferring_client]
   334	                $rd client reply off
   335	                for {set j 0} {$j < $n} {incr j} {
   336	                    set val "$dummy_script[format "%06d" $j]"
   337	                    $rd script load $val
   338	                    $rd set k$j $val
   339	                    if {$j % 1000 == 999} {client_reply_off_wait_for_server $rd}
   340	                }
   341	            } fragment {
   342	                # Delete all the keys to create fragmentation
   343	                for {set j 0} {$j < $n} {incr j} {
   344	                    $rd del k$j
   345	                    if {$j % 1000 == 999} {client_reply_off_wait_for_server $rd}
   346	                }
   347	                $rd close
   348	            }
   349	        }
   350	    }

   352	    proc test_big_hash {type} {
   353	        set title "Active Defrag big hash: $type"
   354	        test $title {
   355	            # number of total fields.  hashes are progressively increasing sizes.
   356	            set n 200000
   357	
   358	            perform_defrag_test $title populate {
   359	                set rd [valkey_deferring_client]
   360	                $rd client reply off
   361	                set val [string repeat A 250]
   362	                set k 0
   363	                set f 0
   364	                for {set j 0} {$j < $n} {incr j} {
   365	                    $rd hset k$k f$f $val
   366	                    lassign [next_exp_kf $k $f] k f
   367	                    if {$j % 1000 == 999} {client_reply_off_wait_for_server $rd}
   368	                }

commit 70d336d892297d1a5e208bee6fc18df363d2ac5e
Author: Seungmin Lee <155032684+sungming2@users.noreply.github.com>
Date:   Thu Aug 7 09:24:47 2025 -0700

    Increase latency for big list test in defrag (#2421)
    
    Across multiple runs of the big list test in defrag, the latency check
    is tripping because the maximum observed defrag cycle latency
    occasionally spikes above our 5 ms limit. While most cycles complete in
    just a few milliseconds, rare slowdowns push some cycles into the double
    digit millisecond range, so a 5 ms hard cap is too aggressive for stable
    testing.
    
    ```
    /runtest --verbose --tls --single unit/memefficiency --only '/big list' --accurate --loop --fastfail
    ```
    
    ```
    [err]: Active Defrag big list: standalone in tests/unit/memefficiency.tcl
    Expected 12 <= 5 (context: type proc line 18 cmd {assert {$max_latency <= $limit_ms}} proc ::validate_latency level 1)
    (Fast fail: test will exit now)
    
    [err]: Active Defrag big list: standalone in tests/unit/memefficiency.tcl
    ```

   376	/* returns 0 if no more work needs to be been done, and 1 if time is up and more work is needed. */
   377	static long scanLaterList(robj *ob, unsigned long *cursor, monotime endtime) {
   378	    quicklist *ql = ob->ptr;
   379	    quicklistNode *node;
   380	    serverAssert(ob->type == OBJ_LIST && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_QUICKLIST);
   381	
   382	    /* Find starting node */
   383	    if (*cursor == 0) {
   384	        node = ql->head;
   385	    } else {
   386	        node = quicklistBookmarkFind(ql, "_AD");
   387	        if (!node) {
   388	            *cursor = 0;
   389	            return 0; /* either bookmark failed to create or deleted, skip this one and continue with other quicklists*/
   390	        }
   391	        node = node->next;
   392	    }
   393	
   394	    /* Process nodes until time expires or list ends */
   395	    while (node) {
   396	        activeDefragQuickListNode(ql, &node);
   397	        server.stat_active_defrag_scanned++;
   398	
   399	        /* Check time limit after processing each node */
   400	        if (getMonotonicUs() > endtime) {
   401	            if (quicklistBookmarkCreate(&ql, "_AD", node)) {
   402	                ob->ptr = ql; /* bookmark creation may have re-allocated the quicklist */
   403	                (*cursor)++;
   404	                return 1;
   405	            }
   406	            break; /* bookmark creation failed - skip this one and continue with other quicklists */
   407	        }
   408	        node = node->next;
   409	    }
   410	
   411	    /* Completed processing all nodes */
   412	    quicklistBookmarkDelete(ql, "_AD");
   413	    *cursor = 0;
   414	    return 0;
   415	}

   528	/* returns 0 if no more work needs to be been done, and 1 if time is up and more work is needed. */
   529	static int scanLaterStreamListpacks(robj *ob, unsigned long *cursor, monotime endtime) {
   530	    static unsigned char last[sizeof(streamID)];
   531	    raxIterator ri;
   532	    long iterations = 0;
   533	    serverAssert(ob->type == OBJ_STREAM && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_STREAM);
   534	
   535	    stream *s = ob->ptr;
   536	    raxStart(&ri, s->rax);
   537	    if (*cursor == 0) {
   538	        /* if cursor is 0, we start new iteration */
   539	        defragRaxNode(&s->rax->head);
   540	        /* assign the iterator node callback before the seek, so that the
   541	         * initial nodes that are processed till the first item are covered */
   542	        ri.node_cb = defragRaxNode;
   543	        raxSeek(&ri, "^", NULL, 0);
   544	    } else {
   545	        /* if cursor is non-zero, we seek to the static 'last' */
   546	        if (!raxSeek(&ri, ">", last, sizeof(last))) {
   547	            *cursor = 0;
   548	            raxStop(&ri);
   549	            return 0;
   550	        }
   551	        /* assign the iterator node callback after the seek, so that the
   552	         * initial nodes that are processed till now aren't covered */
   553	        ri.node_cb = defragRaxNode;
   554	    }
   555	
   556	    (*cursor)++;
   557	    while (raxNext(&ri)) {
   558	        void *newdata = activeDefragAlloc(ri.data);
   559	        if (newdata) raxSetData(ri.node, ri.data = newdata);
   560	        server.stat_active_defrag_scanned++;
   561	        if (++iterations > 128) {
   562	            if (getMonotonicUs() > endtime) {
   563	                serverAssert(ri.key_len == sizeof(last));
   564	                memcpy(last, ri.key, ri.key_len);
   565	                raxStop(&ri);
   566	                return 1;
   567	            }
   568	            iterations = 0;
   569	        }
   570	    }
   571	    raxStop(&ri);
   572	    *cursor = 0;
   573	    return 0;
   574	}
   575	
   576	/* optional callback used defrag each rax element (not including the element pointer itself) */
   577	typedef void *(raxDefragFunction)(raxIterator *ri, void *privdata);
   578	
   579	/* defrag radix tree including:
   580	 * 1) rax struct
   581	 * 2) rax nodes
   582	 * 3) rax entry data (only if defrag_data is specified)
   583	 * 4) call a callback per element, and allow the callback to return a new pointer for the element */
   584	static void defragRadixTree(rax **raxref, int defrag_data, raxDefragFunction *element_cb, void *element_cb_data) {
   585	    raxIterator ri;
   586	    rax *rax;
   587	    if ((rax = activeDefragAlloc(*raxref))) *raxref = rax;
   588	    rax = *raxref;
   589	    raxStart(&ri, rax);
   590	    ri.node_cb = defragRaxNode;
   591	    defragRaxNode(&rax->head);
   592	    raxSeek(&ri, "^", NULL, 0);
   593	    while (raxNext(&ri)) {
   594	        void *newdata = NULL;
   595	        if (element_cb) newdata = element_cb(&ri, element_cb_data);
   596	        if (defrag_data && !newdata) newdata = activeDefragAlloc(ri.data);
   597	        if (newdata) raxSetData(ri.node, ri.data = newdata);
   598	    }
   599	    raxStop(&ri);
   600	}

   788	/* returns 0 more work may or may not be needed (see non-zero cursor),
   789	 * and 1 if time is up and more work is needed. */
   790	static int defragLaterItem(robj *ob, unsigned long *cursor, monotime endtime, int dbid) {
   791	    if (ob) {
   792	        if (ob->type == OBJ_LIST && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_QUICKLIST) {
   793	            return scanLaterList(ob, cursor, endtime);
   794	        } else if (ob->type == OBJ_SET && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_HASHTABLE) {
   795	            scanLaterSet(ob, cursor);
   796	        } else if (ob->type == OBJ_ZSET && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_SKIPLIST) {
   797	            scanLaterZset(ob, cursor);
   798	        } else if (ob->type == OBJ_HASH && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_HASHTABLE) {
   799	            scanLaterHash(ob, cursor);
   800	        } else if (ob->type == OBJ_STREAM && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_STREAM) {
   801	            return scanLaterStreamListpacks(ob, cursor, endtime);
   802	        } else if (ob->type == OBJ_MODULE) {
   803	            /* Fun fact (and a bug since forever): The key is passed to
   804	             * moduleLateDefrag as an sds string, but the parameter is declared
   805	             * to be an robj and it's passed as such to the module type defrag
   806	             * callbacks. Nobody can ever have used this, i.e. accessed the key
   807	             * name in the defrag module type callback. */
   808	            void *sds_key_passed_as_robj = objectGetKey(ob);
   809	            return moduleLateDefrag(sds_key_passed_as_robj, ob, cursor, endtime, dbid);
   810	        } else {
   811	            *cursor = 0; /* object type/encoding may have changed since we schedule it for later */
   812	        }
   813	    } else {
   814	        *cursor = 0; /* object may have been deleted already */
   815	    }
   816	    return 0;
   817	}

   820	// A kvstoreHelperPreContinueFn
   821	static doneStatus defragLaterStep(monotime endtime, void *privdata) {
   822	    defragKeysCtx *ctx = privdata;
   823	
   824	    unsigned int iterations = 0;
   825	    unsigned long long prev_defragged = server.stat_active_defrag_hits;
   826	    unsigned long long prev_scanned = server.stat_active_defrag_scanned;
   827	
   828	    while (defrag_later && listLength(defrag_later) > 0) {
   829	        listNode *head = listFirst(defrag_later);
   830	        sds key = head->value;
   831	        void *found = NULL;
   832	        kvstoreHashtableFind(ctx->kvstate.kvs, ctx->kvstate.slot, key, &found);
   833	        robj *ob = found;
   834	
   835	        long long key_defragged = server.stat_active_defrag_hits;
   836	        bool timeout = (defragLaterItem(ob, &defrag_later_cursor, endtime, ctx->dbid) == 1);
   837	        if (key_defragged != server.stat_active_defrag_hits) {
   838	            server.stat_active_defrag_key_hits++;
   839	        } else {
   840	            server.stat_active_defrag_key_misses++;
   841	        }
   842	
   843	        if (timeout) break;
   844	
   845	        if (defrag_later_cursor == 0) {
   846	            // the item is finished, move on
   847	            listDelNode(defrag_later, head);
   848	        }
   849	
   850	        if (++iterations > 16 || server.stat_active_defrag_hits - prev_defragged > 512 ||
   851	            server.stat_active_defrag_scanned - prev_scanned > 64) {
   852	            if (getMonotonicUs() > endtime) break;
   853	            iterations = 0;
   854	            prev_defragged = server.stat_active_defrag_hits;
   855	            prev_scanned = server.stat_active_defrag_scanned;
   856	        }
   857	    }
   858	
   859	    return (!defrag_later || listLength(defrag_later) == 0) ? DEFRAG_DONE : DEFRAG_NOT_DONE;
   860	}

   866	static doneStatus defragStageKvstoreHelper(monotime endtime,
   867	                                           kvstore *kvs,
   868	                                           hashtableScanFunction scan_fn,
   869	                                           kvstoreHelperPreContinueFn precontinue_fn,
   870	                                           void *privdata) {
   871	    static kvstoreIterState state; // STATIC - this persists
   872	    if (endtime == 0) {
   873	        // Starting the stage, set up the state information for this stage
   874	        state.kvs = kvs;
   875	        state.slot = KVS_SLOT_DEFRAG_LUT;
   876	        state.cursor = 0;
   877	        return DEFRAG_NOT_DONE;
   878	    }
   879	    if (kvs != state.kvs) {
   880	        // There has been a change of the kvs (flushdb, swapdb, etc.).  Just complete the stage.
   881	        return DEFRAG_DONE;
   882	    }
   883	
   884	    unsigned int iterations = 0;
   885	    unsigned long long prev_defragged = server.stat_active_defrag_hits;
   886	    unsigned long long prev_scanned = server.stat_active_defrag_scanned;
   887	
   888	    if (state.slot == KVS_SLOT_DEFRAG_LUT) {
   889	        // Before we start scanning the kvstore, handle the main structures
   890	        do {
   891	            state.cursor = kvstoreHashtableDefragTables(kvs, state.cursor, activeDefragAlloc);
   892	            if (getMonotonicUs() >= endtime) return DEFRAG_NOT_DONE;
   893	        } while (state.cursor != 0);
   894	        state.slot = KVS_SLOT_UNASSIGNED;
   895	    }
   896	
   897	    while (true) {
   898	        if (++iterations > 16 || server.stat_active_defrag_hits - prev_defragged > 512 || server.stat_active_defrag_scanned - prev_scanned > 64) {
   899	            if (getMonotonicUs() >= endtime) break;
   900	            iterations = 0;
   901	            prev_defragged = server.stat_active_defrag_hits;
   902	            prev_scanned = server.stat_active_defrag_scanned;
   903	        }
   904	
   905	        if (precontinue_fn) {
   906	            if (privdata) *(kvstoreIterState *)privdata = state;
   907	            if (precontinue_fn(endtime, privdata) == DEFRAG_NOT_DONE) return DEFRAG_NOT_DONE;
   908	        }
   909	
   910	        if (!state.cursor) {
   911	            // If there's no cursor, we're ready to begin a new kvstore slot.
   912	            if (state.slot == KVS_SLOT_UNASSIGNED) {
   913	                state.slot = kvstoreGetFirstNonEmptyHashtableIndex(kvs);
   914	            } else {
   915	                state.slot = kvstoreGetNextNonEmptyHashtableIndex(kvs, state.slot);
   916	            }
   917	
   918	            if (state.slot == KVS_SLOT_UNASSIGNED) return DEFRAG_DONE;
   919	        }
   920	
   921	        // Whatever privdata's actual type, this function requires that it begins with kvstoreIterState.
   922	        if (privdata) *(kvstoreIterState *)privdata = state;
   923	        state.cursor = kvstoreHashtableScanDefrag(kvs, state.slot, state.cursor,
   924	                                                  scan_fn, privdata, activeDefragAlloc,
   925	                                                  HASHTABLE_SCAN_EMIT_REF);
   926	    }
   927	
   928	    return DEFRAG_NOT_DONE;
   929	}

   602	typedef struct {
   603	    streamCG *cg;
   604	    streamConsumer *c;
   605	} PendingEntryContext;
   606	
   607	static void *defragStreamConsumerPendingEntry(raxIterator *ri, void *privdata) {
   608	    PendingEntryContext *ctx = privdata;
   609	    streamNACK *nack = ri->data, *newnack;
   610	    nack->consumer = ctx->c; /* update nack pointer to consumer */
   611	    newnack = activeDefragAlloc(nack);
   612	    if (newnack) {
   613	        /* update consumer group pointer to the nack */
   614	        void *prev;
   615	        raxInsert(ctx->cg->pel, ri->key, ri->key_len, newnack, &prev);
   616	        serverAssert(prev == nack);
   617	    }
   618	    return newnack;
   619	}
   620	
   621	static void *defragStreamConsumer(raxIterator *ri, void *privdata) {
   622	    streamConsumer *c = ri->data;
   623	    streamCG *cg = privdata;
   624	    void *newc = activeDefragAlloc(c);
   625	    if (newc) {
   626	        c = newc;
   627	    }
   628	    sds newsds = activeDefragSds(c->name);
   629	    if (newsds) c->name = newsds;
   630	    if (c->pel) {
   631	        PendingEntryContext pel_ctx = {cg, c};
   632	        defragRadixTree(&c->pel, 0, defragStreamConsumerPendingEntry, &pel_ctx);
   633	    }
   634	    return newc; /* returns NULL if c was not defragged */
   635	}
   636	
   637	static void *defragStreamConsumerGroup(raxIterator *ri, void *privdata) {
   638	    streamCG *cg = ri->data;
   639	    UNUSED(privdata);
   640	    if (cg->consumers) defragRadixTree(&cg->consumers, 0, defragStreamConsumer, cg);
   641	    if (cg->pel) defragRadixTree(&cg->pel, 0, NULL, NULL);
   642	    return NULL;
   643	}

   645	static void defragStream(robj *ob) {
   646	    serverAssert(ob->type == OBJ_STREAM && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_STREAM);
   647	    stream *s = ob->ptr, *news;
   648	
   649	    /* handle the main struct */
   650	    if ((news = activeDefragAlloc(s))) ob->ptr = s = news;
   651	
   652	    if (raxSize(s->rax) > server.active_defrag_max_scan_fields) {
   653	        rax *newrax = activeDefragAlloc(s->rax);
   654	        if (newrax) s->rax = newrax;
   655	        defragLater(ob);
   656	    } else
   657	        defragRadixTree(&s->rax, 1, NULL, NULL);
   658	
   659	    if (s->cgroups) defragRadixTree(&s->cgroups, 1, defragStreamConsumerGroup, NULL);
   660	}

   662	/* Defrag a module key. This is either done immediately or scheduled
   663	 * for later. Returns then number of pointers defragged.
   664	 */
   665	static void defragModule(serverDb *db, robj *obj) {
   666	    serverAssert(obj->type == OBJ_MODULE);
   667	    /* Fun fact (and a bug since forever): The key is passed to
   668	     * moduleDefragValue as an sds string, but the parameter is declared to be
   669	     * an robj and it's passed as such to the module type defrag callbacks.
   670	     * Nobody can ever have used this, i.e. accessed the key name in the defrag
   671	     * or free_effort module type callbacks. */
   672	    void *sds_key_passed_as_robj = objectGetKey(obj);
   673	    if (!moduleDefragValue(sds_key_passed_as_robj, obj, db->id)) defragLater(obj);
   674	}

   676	/* for each key we scan in the main dict, this function will attempt to defrag
   677	 * all the various pointers it has. */
   678	static void defragKey(defragKeysCtx *ctx, robj **elemref) {
   679	    serverDb *db = server.db[ctx->dbid];
   680	    int slot = ctx->kvstate.slot;
   681	    robj *newob, *ob;
   682	    unsigned char *newzl;
   683	    ob = *elemref;
   684	
   685	    /* Try to defrag robj and/or string value. */
   686	    if ((newob = activeDefragStringOb(ob))) {
   687	        *elemref = newob;
   688	        if (objectGetExpire(newob) >= 0) {
   689	            /* Replace the pointer in the expire table without accessing the old
   690	             * pointer. */
   691	            hashtable *expires_ht = kvstoreGetHashtable(db->expires, slot);
   692	            bool replaced = hashtableReplaceReallocatedEntry(expires_ht, ob, newob);
   693	            serverAssert(replaced);
   694	        }
   695	        if (newob->type == OBJ_HASH && hashTypeHasVolatileFields(newob)) {
   696	            /* Check if this is a hash object containing volatile fields.
   697	             * and update keys_with_volatile_items after defrag. */
   698	            hashtable *keys_with_volatile_items_ht = kvstoreGetHashtable(db->keys_with_volatile_items, slot);
   699	            bool replaced = hashtableReplaceReallocatedEntry(keys_with_volatile_items_ht, ob, newob);
   700	            serverAssert(replaced);
   701	        }
   702	        ob = newob;
   703	    }
   704	
   705	    if (ob->type == OBJ_STRING) {
   706	        /* Already handled in activeDefragStringOb. */
   707	    } else if (ob->type == OBJ_LIST) {
   708	        if (ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_QUICKLIST) {
   709	            defragQuicklist(ob);
   710	        } else if (ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_LISTPACK) {
   711	            if ((newzl = activeDefragAlloc(ob->ptr))) ob->ptr = newzl;
   712	        } else {
   713	            serverPanic("Unknown list encoding");
   714	        }
   715	    } else if (ob->type == OBJ_SET) {
   716	        if (ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_HASHTABLE) {
   717	            defragSet(ob);
   718	        } else if (ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_INTSET || ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_LISTPACK) {
   719	            void *newptr, *ptr = ob->ptr;
   720	            if ((newptr = activeDefragAlloc(ptr))) ob->ptr = newptr;
   721	        } else {
   722	            serverPanic("Unknown set encoding");
   723	        }
   724	    } else if (ob->type == OBJ_ZSET) {
   725	        if (ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_LISTPACK) {
   726	            if ((newzl = activeDefragAlloc(ob->ptr))) ob->ptr = newzl;
   727	        } else if (ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_SKIPLIST) {
   728	            defragZsetSkiplist(ob);
   729	        } else {
   730	            serverPanic("Unknown sorted set encoding");
   731	        }
   732	    } else if (ob->type == OBJ_HASH) {
   733	        defragHash(ob);
   734	    } else if (ob->type == OBJ_STREAM) {
   735	        defragStream(ob);
   736	    } else if (ob->type == OBJ_MODULE) {
   737	        defragModule(db, ob);
   738	    } else {
   739	        serverPanic("Unknown object type");
   740	    }
   741	}

   743	/* Defrag scan callback for the main db dictionary. */
   744	static void dbKeysScanCallback(void *privdata, void *elemref) {
   745	    long long hits_before = server.stat_active_defrag_hits;
   746	    defragKey((defragKeysCtx *)privdata, (robj **)elemref);
   747	    if (server.stat_active_defrag_hits != hits_before)
   748	        server.stat_active_defrag_key_hits++;
   749	    else
   750	        server.stat_active_defrag_key_misses++;
   751	    server.stat_active_defrag_scanned++;
   752	}

   754	/* Defrag scan callback for a pubsub channels hashtable. */
   755	static void defragPubsubScanCallback(void *privdata, void *elemref) {
   756	    defragPubSubCtx *ctx = privdata;
   757	    void **clients_ref = (void **)elemref;
   758	    hashtable *newclients, *clients = *clients_ref;
   759	    robj *newchannel, *channel = *(robj **)hashtableMetadata(clients);
   760	
   761	    /* Try to defrag the channel name. */
   762	    serverAssert(channel->refcount == (int)hashtableSize(clients) + 1);
   763	    newchannel = activeDefragStringOb(channel);
   764	    if (newchannel) {
   765	        *(robj **)hashtableMetadata(clients) = newchannel;
   766	
   767	        /* The channel name is shared by the client's pubsub(shard) and server's
   768	         * pubsub(shard), after defraging the channel name, we need to update
   769	         * the reference in the clients' dictionary. */
   770	        hashtableIterator iter;
   771	        hashtableInitIterator(&iter, clients, 0);
   772	        void *c;
   773	        while (hashtableNext(&iter, &c)) {
   774	            hashtable *client_channels = ctx->getPubSubChannels(c);
   775	            bool replaced = hashtableReplaceReallocatedEntry(client_channels, channel, newchannel);
   776	            serverAssert(replaced);
   777	        }
   778	        hashtableResetIterator(&iter);
   779	    }
   780	
   781	    /* Try to defrag the dictionary of clients that is stored as the value part. */
   782	    if ((newclients = hashtableDefragTables(clients, activeDefragAlloc)))
   783	        *clients_ref = newclients;
   784	
   785	    server.stat_active_defrag_scanned++;
   786	}

   447	static void defragQuicklist(robj *ob) {
   448	    quicklist *ql = ob->ptr, *newql;
   449	    serverAssert(ob->type == OBJ_LIST && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_QUICKLIST);
   450	    if ((newql = activeDefragAlloc(ql))) ob->ptr = ql = newql;
   451	    if (ql->len > server.active_defrag_max_scan_fields)
   452	        defragLater(ob);
   453	    else
   454	        activeDefragQuickListNodes(ql);
   455	}
   456	
   457	static void defragZsetSkiplist(robj *ob) {
   458	    serverAssert(ob->type == OBJ_ZSET && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_SKIPLIST);
   459	    zset *zs = (zset *)ob->ptr;
   460	
   461	    zset *newzs;
   462	    zskiplist *newzsl;
   463	    struct zskiplistNode *newheader;
   464	    if ((newzs = activeDefragAlloc(zs))) ob->ptr = zs = newzs;
   465	    if ((newzsl = activeDefragAlloc(zs->zsl))) zs->zsl = newzsl;
   466	    if ((newheader = activeDefragAlloc(zs->zsl->header))) zs->zsl->header = newheader;
   467	
   468	    hashtable *newtable;
   469	    if ((newtable = hashtableDefragTables(zs->ht, activeDefragAlloc))) zs->ht = newtable;
   470	
   471	    if (hashtableSize(zs->ht) > server.active_defrag_max_scan_fields)
   472	        defragLater(ob);
   473	    else {
   474	        unsigned long cursor = 0;
   475	        do {
   476	            cursor = hashtableScanDefrag(zs->ht, cursor, activeDefragZsetNode, zs->zsl, activeDefragAlloc, HASHTABLE_SCAN_EMIT_REF);
   477	        } while (cursor != 0);
   478	    }
   479	}
   480	
   481	/* Defragment a hash object.
   482	 *
   483	 * Large hashtable-encoded hashes are deferred via `defrag_later`.
   484	 * Smaller ones are defragmented immediately, possibly over multiple passes.
   485	 * Listpack-encoded hashes are always handled in a single pass. */
   486	static void defragHash(robj *ob) {
   487	    hashtable *ht = ob->ptr;
   488	    if (ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_HASHTABLE && hashtableSize(ht) > server.active_defrag_max_scan_fields) {
   489	        /* Large hashtable-encoded hashes are deferred via `defrag_later` */
   490	        defragLater(ob);
   491	    } else {
   492	        /* Smaller hashtables are defragmented immediately, possibly over multiple passes.
   493	         * Listpack-encoded hashes are always handled in a single pass in hashTypeScanDefrag. */
   494	        unsigned long cursor = 0;
   495	        do {
   496	            cursor = hashTypeScanDefrag(ob, cursor, activeDefragAlloc);
   497	        } while (cursor != 0);
   498	    }
   499	}
   500	
   501	static void defragSet(robj *ob) {
   502	    serverAssert(ob->type == OBJ_SET && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_HASHTABLE);
   503	    hashtable *ht = ob->ptr;
   504	    if (hashtableSize(ht) > server.active_defrag_max_scan_fields) {
   505	        defragLater(ob);
   506	    } else {
   507	        unsigned long cursor = 0;
   508	        do {
   509	            cursor = hashtableScanDefrag(ht, cursor, activeDefragSdsHashtableCallback, NULL, activeDefragAlloc, HASHTABLE_SCAN_EMIT_REF);
   510	        } while (cursor != 0);
   511	    }
   512	    /* defrag the hashtable struct and tables */
   513	    hashtable *new_hashtable = hashtableDefragTables(ht, activeDefragAlloc);
   514	    if (new_hashtable) ob->ptr = new_hashtable;
   515	}
   516	
   517	/* Defrag callback for radix tree iterator, called for each node,
   518	 * used in order to defrag the nodes allocations. */
   519	static int defragRaxNode(raxNode **noderef) {
   520	    raxNode *newnode = activeDefragAlloc(*noderef);
   521	    if (newnode) {
   522	        *noderef = newnode;
   523	        return 1;
   524	    }
   525	    return 0;
   526	}

I see - `hashtableScanDefrag` processes a single bucket chain at a time. The issue is that `scanLaterSet`, `scanLaterZset`, and `scanLaterHash` call `hashtableScanDefrag` once per defrag cycle without checking time limits. If a bucket chain is very long (many child buckets due to collisions), this could cause a latency spike.

But wait, let me look at the `defragLaterStep` function more carefully. It loops through items in `defrag_later` and calls `defragLaterItem` for each. For `scanLaterSet`, `scanLaterZset`, and `scanLaterHash`, these don't check the endtime and always return 0 (not timeout). So `defragLaterStep` will continue processing more items from `defrag_later` until either:
1. `defrag_later` is empty
2. Timeout from `scanLaterList` or `scanLaterStreamListpacks`
3. The iteration count check at line 850-852

Let me look at the iteration count logic more carefully:

```c
if (++iterations > 16 || server.stat_active_defrag_hits - prev_defragged > 512 ||
    server.stat_active_defrag_scanned - prev_scanned > 64) {
    if (getMonotonicUs() > endtime) break;
```

This means it will process at most 16 items from `defrag_later` before checking time. But wait, for set/zset/hash items, each `hashtableScanDefrag` call processes one bucket chain. For large hash tables, a single bucket chain could have many entries and many child buckets.

Let me check the `scanLaterZset` more carefully:

```c
static void scanLaterZset(robj *ob, unsigned long *cursor) {
    serverAssert(ob->type == OBJ_ZSET && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_SKIPLIST);
    zset *zs = (zset *)ob->ptr;
    *cursor = hashtableScanDefrag(zs->ht, *cursor, scanLaterZsetCallback, zs->zsl, activeDefragAlloc, HASHTABLE_SCAN_EMIT_REF);
}
```

Each call to `hashtableScanDefrag` processes one bucket chain. For a zset with a large hash table, each bucket chain should be relatively small (the hash table grows to keep bucket chains small). So the latency per call should be bounded.

But wait, the `scanLaterZsetCallback` calls `activeDefragZsetNode` which does a skiplist lookup to find update pointers - that's O(log N) for each node. For a large zset, this could take significant time per node.

Now I see the problem clearly. The PR description says: "We implemented a temporary fix in https://github.com/valkey-io/valkey/pull/2421/files, but we should investigate how to return the latency to < 5ms."

The temporary fix was raising the latency limit to 40ms in the test. The actual fix (which we need to implement) involves changes to the source code to reduce latency. From the commit history, I can see two key changes:

1. `84fd62641` - Refactor `scanLaterList` to fix latency issue (already applied)
2. `d7fb76665` - Reduce active defrag test latency by lowering hit threshold (NOT yet applied)

The changes in `d7fb76665` are:
1. Change `prev_defragged` type from `unsigned long long` to `long long` (cosmetic)
2. Change `server.stat_active_defrag_hits - prev_defragged > 512` to `server.stat_active_defrag_hits > prev_defragged` (i.e., check if ANY defrag happened, not just > 512)
3. Change latency limit back from 40 to 5 in test

This makes sense! The issue is that previously, the code would check for time only after 512 defrag hits. If defrag hits were happening slowly (but the work was still CPU-intensive), the code wouldn't check the time frequently enough, causing latency spikes. By changing the threshold to check after ANY defrag hit, the code yields more frequently.

   528	/* returns 0 if no more work needs to be been done, and 1 if time is up and more work is needed. */
   529	static int scanLaterStreamListpacks(robj *ob, unsigned long *cursor, monotime endtime) {
   530	    static unsigned char last[sizeof(streamID)];
   531	    raxIterator ri;
   532	    long iterations = 0;
   533	    serverAssert(ob->type == OBJ_STREAM && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_STREAM);
   534	
   535	    stream *s = ob->ptr;
   536	    raxStart(&ri, s->rax);
   537	    if (*cursor == 0) {
   538	        /* if cursor is 0, we start new iteration */
   539	        defragRaxNode(&s->rax->head);
   540	        /* assign the iterator node callback before the seek, so that the
   541	         * initial nodes that are processed till the first item are covered */
   542	        ri.node_cb = defragRaxNode;
   543	        raxSeek(&ri, "^", NULL, 0);
   544	    } else {
   545	        /* if cursor is non-zero, we seek to the static 'last' */
   546	        if (!raxSeek(&ri, ">", last, sizeof(last))) {
   547	            *cursor = 0;
   548	            raxStop(&ri);
   549	            return 0;
   550	        }
   551	        /* assign the iterator node callback after the seek, so that the
   552	         * initial nodes that are processed till now aren't covered */
   553	        ri.node_cb = defragRaxNode;
   554	    }
   555	
   556	    (*cursor)++;
   557	    while (raxNext(&ri)) {
   558	        void *newdata = activeDefragAlloc(ri.data);
   559	        if (newdata) raxSetData(ri.node, ri.data = newdata);
   560	        server.stat_active_defrag_scanned++;
   561	        if (++iterations > 128) {
   562	            if (getMonotonicUs() > endtime) {
   563	                serverAssert(ri.key_len == sizeof(last));
   564	                memcpy(last, ri.key, ri.key_len);
   565	                raxStop(&ri);
   566	                return 1;
   567	            }
   568	            iterations = 0;
   569	        }
   570	    }
   571	    raxStop(&ri);
   572	    *cursor = 0;
   573	    return 0;
   574	}
   575

The `scanLaterStreamListpacks` function processes 128 items before checking the time. While each `activeDefragAlloc` call should be fast, 128 iterations could still add up. But this is probably less of an issue than the main problem.

Let me now look at the `scanLaterSet`, `scanLaterZset`, and `scanLaterHash` functions to see if they need time limit checks too. But first, let me understand: these functions are called from `defragLaterItem` which is called from `defragLaterStep`. The issue is that `defragLaterStep` has a check for `server.stat_active_defrag_hits - prev_defragged > 512` which means it may process many items before checking time if defrag hits are slow.

Now let me implement the changes. The key changes are:

1. In `defragLaterStep`: Change the condition from `server.stat_active_defrag_hits - prev_defragged > 512` to `server.stat_active_defrag_hits > prev_defragged` (check after any hit)
2. In `defragStageKvstoreHelper`: Same change
3. Change `prev_defragged` type from `unsigned long long` to `long long` to match the actual type

Additionally, looking at `scanLaterStreamListpacks`, I should also reduce the batch size from 128 to a smaller number or check time on every iteration.

static int scanLaterStreamListpacks(robj *ob, unsigned long *cursor, monotime endtime) {
    static unsigned char last[sizeof(streamID)];
    raxIterator ri;
    long iterations = 0;
    serverAssert(ob->type == OBJ_STREAM && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_STREAM);

    stream *s = ob->ptr;
    raxStart(&ri, s->rax);
    if (*cursor == 0) {
        /* if cursor is 0, we start new iteration */
        defragRaxNode(&s->rax->head);
        /* assign the iterator node callback before the seek, so that the
         * initial nodes that are processed till the first item are covered */
        ri.node_cb = defragRaxNode;
        raxSeek(&ri, "^", NULL, 0);
    } else {
        /* if cursor is non-zero, we seek to the static '"'"'last'"'"' */

            *cursor = 0;
            raxStop(&ri);
            return 0;

         * initial nodes that are processed till now aren'"'"'t covered */
        ri.node_cb = defragRaxNode;

The code compiles successfully. Now let me also check if there are any other places that need changes. Let me look at the `scanLaterZset` function and the `scanLaterSet` function to see if they need time checks:

The `scanLaterSet` function:
```c
static void scanLaterSet(robj *ob, unsigned long *cursor) {
    hashtable *ht = ob->ptr;
    *cursor = hashtableScanDefrag(ht, *cursor, activeDefragSdsHashtableCallback, NULL, activeDefragAlloc, HASHTABLE_SCAN_EMIT_REF);
}
```

This processes one bucket chain per call. The bucket chain should be bounded in size (the hashtable implementation limits bucket chain length). So each call should be fast.

Similarly for `scanLaterHash` and `scanLaterZset`.

But wait, there's another potential issue. The `scanLaterZset` function uses `scanLaterZsetCallback` which calls `activeDefragZsetNode`. That function does a skiplist traversal for each node, which could be O(log N) per node. If a single bucket has many entries, this could be slow. But again, bucket chains should be short.

Let me also check if `scanLaterSet` and `scanLaterHash` need time limit checks. These functions are called from `defragLaterItem` which doesn't pass `endtime` to them. Let me check if they should:

Looking at `defragLaterItem`:
```c
static int defragLaterItem(robj *ob, unsigned long *cursor, monotime endtime, int dbid) {
    if (ob) {
        if (ob->type == OBJ_LIST && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_QUICKLIST) {
            return scanLaterList(ob, cursor, endtime);
        } else if (ob->type == OBJ_SET && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_HASHTABLE) {
            scanLaterSet(ob, cursor);
        } else if (ob->type == OBJ_ZSET && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_SKIPLIST) {
            scanLaterZset(ob, cursor);
        } else if (ob->type == OBJ_HASH && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_HASHTABLE) {
            scanLaterHash(ob, cursor);
        } else if (ob->type == OBJ_STREAM && ob->encoding == OBJ_ENCODING_STREAM) {
            return scanLaterStreamListpacks(ob, cursor, endtime);
        ...
```

Only `scanLaterList` and `scanLaterStreamListpacks` check the time and return 1 when time is up. The others (`scanLaterSet`, `scanLaterZset`, `scanLaterHash`) don't check time and always return 0 (via the default at the end of the function). This means that when processing a set, zset, or hash item from the defrag_later list, the time won't be checked until the loop in `defragLaterStep` hits its iteration limit.

But with our change, `defragLaterStep` now checks after every defrag hit (`server.stat_active_defrag_hits > prev_defragged`), so even if `scanLaterSet`/`scanLaterZset`/`scanLaterHash` don't check time, the outer loop will catch it after each bucket chain that results in a defrag.

However, if no defrag happens (i.e., the allocator decides not to move memory), the loop could continue for many iterations. But the `iterations > 16` check handles this - after 16 iterations, it checks the time.

So the changes I made should be sufficient. But let me also think about whether `scanLaterSet`, `scanLaterZset`, and `scanLaterHash` should also get time limit checks. Looking at the commit `84fd62641` which fixed `scanLaterList`, it added time checks. But similar checks weren't added to the other scanLater functions because... hmm, let me think.

Actually, for `scanLaterSet`, `scanLaterZset`, and `scanLaterHash`, each call processes one bucket chain, which should be fast. The outer loop in `defragLaterStep` provides enough time checking granularity with our fix. The `scanLaterList` function was special because it could process many nodes in a single call (without the fix, it would process the entire list in one go). Similarly, `scanLaterStreamListpacks` could process many entries.

So the changes I made should be good.

Now let me think about edge cases:

1. **No defrag hits scenario**: If the allocator doesn't find any memory to defrag, `server.stat_active_defrag_hits` won't increment. Our change uses `server.stat_active_defrag_hits > prev_defragged` instead of `server.stat_active_defrag_hits - prev_defragged > 512`. This means we still rely on `iterations > 16` to check time, which is fine.

2. **Busy loop prevention**: The `iterations > 16` check ensures we check time at least every 16 iterations, even if no defrag hits occur. This prevents a busy loop.

3. **Type consistency**: `server.stat_active_defrag_hits` is `long long`, so `prev_defragged` should also be `long long` to avoid signed/unsigned comparison issues.

Let me also check if there's a similar issue in the `defragStageKvstoreHelper` function with the `kvstoreHashtableDefragTables` call. Let me look at that:

   908	        }
   909	
   910	        if (!state.cursor) {
   911	            // If there's no cursor, we're ready to begin a new kvstore slot.
   912	            if (state.slot == KVS_SLOT_UNASSIGNED) {
   913	                state.slot = kvstoreGetFirstNonEmptyHashtableIndex(kvs);
   914	            } else {
   915	                state.slot = kvstoreGetNextNonEmptyHashtableIndex(kvs, state.slot);
   916	            }
   917	
   918	            if (state.slot == KVS_SLOT_UNASSIGNED) return DEFRAG_DONE;
   919	        }
   920	
   921	        // Whatever privdata's actual type, this function requires that it begins with kvstoreIterState.
   922	        if (privdata) *(kvstoreIterState *)privdata = state;
   923	        state.cursor = kvstoreHashtableScanDefrag(kvs, state.slot, state.cursor,
   924	                                                  scan_fn, privdata, activeDefragAlloc,
   925	                                                  HASHTABLE_SCAN_EMIT_REF);
   926	    }
   927	
   928	    return DEFRAG_NOT_DONE;
   929	}
